Cauliflower:
This wasn't on the menu but we asked for different veggie options. The spices and flavors used in this stir fry were so good! There are small pieces of pork belly that marinate in the same seasonings. Awesome!

Cumin ribs:
These were soooo tender; the meat just falls off the bone. The outer coating is nice and crispy from the cumin rub. Amazing! Probably my favorite dish.

Mushroom beef fillet mild:
This was ok. It has that kind of greasy soy flavor. It wasn't bad, just not my taste.

Specially tea smoked duck:
This has a nice smokey flavor, almost like a ham but in duck format. The skin is super crispy and thin and not that oily either. This was pretty good! I just wish I could taste more tea flavor.<//Review>

<name>Robert P< /name>< Text>
I lived in Hunan for more than five years. This food tastes the same. It's very authentic. But I only gave four stars because you have to serve yourself water from the water cooler across the room. It would be much better if they left a pitcher of water on the table. For faster service, you have to summon the waiters Chinese style (with a loud voice). Don't be shy. It's just a cultural difference. The prices are reasonable and the portions are large enough. There's plenty of parking outside, but be prepared to wait in line a bit during peak hours. If you like spicy, order the frog.<//Text>

< Pictures>
[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNzHeoetPeh0ygLCo6ddH5Fn0r-G8s4YPhS5TdO=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPKWcX999iVa92_CtwxsUsGe35CGSGeLCIzlUTZ=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNZh6J0GU5DjXSLvI_XiIvDaSyo4NN2mV3kP0-y=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPkG3RGv-39OWz155bS-S2OTATK9b7deqmE_lzw=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pictures>
< text>
Overpriced poor quality food, not at all like in China.  I have visited Beijing, Xi'an, Yichang, Shanghai, and Zhengzhou in China. The restaurants where the locals eat in each of these areas have excellent food prepared by owners who take pride in the quality and preparation of their food.  They serve some of the best food I have ever eaten with large portions, fresh ingredients, and fair prices.  Village Kitchen is the opposite.  The food is bland and every corner is cut to maximize profits.  The lamb pictured in the menu shows chunks, however what is served is miniscule shavings of lamb like the wood shavings from a pencil sharpener.  The only flavor of the lamb dish was an overabundance of cooking oil.  When I got home my body decided to reject the meal from both ends. My wife ordered the pork stomach which was also bland and priced double that of better quality restaurants.  If you are planning to spend at least $50 for two people, a way better meal can be had at the many better Chinese restaurants in San Diego like Chins and Chuns.</text>

<review>This is one of my favorite Chinese places in San Diego, alongside Village North.  They serve Hunan cuisine which is known for its spiciness and unforgiving assault of flavors on the palate, so be prepared for a heavy tasting meal and perhaps lots of rice and ice water!

Some of the highlights here include the preserved pork--I like it both in the stir fry and in the dry pot.  The stir fry can be a tad dry at times, but the fresh garlic leaves more than make up for that, and the dry pot is just so flavorful with the smoked bamboos, giving the dish as smoky of a flavor as you will ever find in Chinese food (which should appeal to any BBQ fans out there).  Chairman Mao's braised pork is quite good, similar to many other braised pork dishes, with a fermented bean curd flavor, as is common in the braised pork of certain Chinese (non Shanghainese) cuisines.  The deboned pork rib with fried egg casserole is actually one of the milder dishes on the menu in terms of flavor, but not in terms of spiciness! It's one that I enjoy very much as well for some lighter dishes to balance the others.  On the other hand, the pickled chilli with pork is quite a spicy dish, with the aromas of the chilli pepper making the dish very very good.

Of the non-pork dishes, the Chef's Beef Brisket is quite good, a little bit reminiscent of beef noodle soups except served as a dish without noodles and soup.  The mapo tofu is a simple but very flavorful dish with plenty of Sichuan peppercorns to numb your tongue.  The steamed egg here is possibly one of my favorite steamed eggs I've had, with some good flavors and a very good texture on the egg--not over or underdone.  The eggplant with green chilli and century egg dish is one of their signatures for a reason.  The flavors are very balanced with the eggplant serving as a good base.

I could probably go on about the other dishes since there really hasn't been many that have disappointed me.  I highly recommend coming with a group of people to order and try more dishes and seeing which you enjoy the most!  I also noticed that the dishes tend to be spicier in the summer, since perhaps it fluctuates with the spiciness of the chilli peppers which may be seasonal, so if you want to give yourself a challenge, definitely come during that time.< /review>< pics>
None</pics>

<Text>This place was recommended by one of our foodie friends so I had decent expectations coming in. I found out later that there was one particular dish he was a fan of - the mashed eggplant with century egg. Comes with a giant mortar and pestle that looked pretty neat and was the best mix of flavors in an eggplant dish I've ever had if not the biggest portion. Most of the other dishes were just average (braised pork), lacking in flavor (fried rice), or just came with a higher price when compared with other places such as Chef Chin or Szechuan Chef.

Since I'm a fan of tea we also tried the Dragon Well and Oosmanthus Oolong teas which looked like they were loose leaf but somehow still lacked flavor, perhaps they had been recycled?

Food did come out quickly though and service was pretty good for a Chinese place - we were in and out in about an hour. If you're really into Hunan cuisine, you might like it more but otherwise I would consider it a maybe try once kind of place.< /Text><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< response>

We recently had to put our beloved dog, Spencer, to sleep. She had been adopted from Woods in 2008 and she was most likely around 15 when she was ready to go. Though we had never met the vet, Dr. Laura Whitelaw, she treated us with such kindness and reverence that I was touched inside of my own grief. She treated it more like a funeral for a beloved family member than anything and made sure to check in with us, and what we wanted while still being professional. I think you can tell a lot from a vet, and a person, when they are asked to put down a pet-- and she stood out as a compassionate animal lover who truly cared about us and our dog. <review>There are, in all the universe, only four reasons to get off Interstate 15 and stop in Victorville.

Perhaps, like me, a loved one lives there. More likely, you need gasoline or a quick hit of meth from one of the many dealers who seem to make up Victorville's primary industry

The fourth reason, and the best reason, to get off the freeway in Victorville is this donut shop.

The donuts are consistently fresh, they don't have that corporate taste, for lack of a better phrase, that you find at Krispy Kreme, and the people who run the place are just as charming as can be.

< Review>
I recently picked up fishing as something to get-out-and-do. I've been on three different fishing tours with three different guides. One was disastrous. Another was much better, which I though was good, until I tried The Long Run Sportfishing (TLRS). I've gone out with them twice now, the first time was hands down the best fishing trip I've been on. The guides were helpful. The fishing was great, caught a yellowfin and later a halibut. The other customers were positive and friendly. The boat, gear, and tackle were all in good order and well kept. But also, the crew were professional while still easygoing and knowledgeable. So I went out again a month later with TLRS. My experience was almost as good, the only difference was the fish weren't as accommodating for the first part of the day. The Captain took us to a different spot which really made a difference to the day. Of course the Captain and the crew can't control the fish or where they will be, but they did a great job with how it all played out.
If you are looking for a one-off fishing trip or if you are looking for more frequent trips with a good organization. I would highly recommend The Long Run Sportfishing as the sport fishing guides to get it done, and done well. Cheers!</Review>
